  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f201514a-b38d-47ac-a7cf-dd12268d002e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText1979636095802485141" style="display:none"><i>He smiles. It's a wicked smile. Kind but not kind. Handsome but dangerous. Feral almost. I can see why Nick nearly killed him, Nick...<br />I ask again, "Why were you in the road?"<br />"I was waiting for you."</i><br /><br />Zara and her friends thought they'd solved the pixie problem. And they did - sort of. The pixie's are all locked away, deep in the woods. But the king's needs grow stronger each day that he is in captivity, while his control over his people weakens. And it's enough to draw a new king into town. Astley claims he is different. He claims there are pixies who can live peacefully with humans, that it doesn't have to be all violence and nastiness all the time. Zara wants to believe him...until Astley also claims that she is fated to be his queen.<br /><br />There is no way Zara would ever turn pixie. And she's got good friends who will make sure of that. Besides, she and Nick are so in love they're practically inseparable. But when they very thing Zara wants to protect most is exactly what's at risk, she is forced to make choices she never imagined...</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_77131150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77131150" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77131150?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Need</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=hated-this-book">hated-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=terrible-writing">terrible-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=hate-this-series">hate-this-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=wtf-is-wrong-with-me">wtf-is-wrong-with-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77131150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7555033650472983690">Captivate picks up where Need left off. <b>The first half of the book is pretty much about building up the importance of Zara's and Nick's relationship and how in love they are. </b>They try to go on with their lives and live normally after imprisoning Zara's Dad and his pixie subjects. More pixies are coming to their town and they can't figure out why. Zara, Nick, Devyn, and Issie all capture the pixies that come to the town and trap them in the house. This is obviously only a temporary solution.<br/><br/><i>Two o</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7555033650472983690" style="display:none">Captivate picks up where Need left off. <b>The first half of the book is pretty much about building up the importance of Zara's and Nick's relationship and how in love they are. </b>They try to go on with their lives and live normally after imprisoning Zara's Dad and his pixie subjects. More pixies are coming to their town and they can't figure out why. Zara, Nick, Devyn, and Issie all capture the pixies that come to the town and trap them in the house. This is obviously only a temporary solution.<br /><br /><i>Two other pixie kings find out that Zara's Dad is imprisoned and weak so they decide they want to kill him and take his territory. Astley is one of the pixie kings and he is actually saved by Zara in the beginning. After meeting him she starts to wonder if all pixies are bad and if the situation is so black and white.</i><br /><br /><b>I had a lot of problems with this book.</b> First off, Nick and Zara's relationship becomes the main focal point for the better half of the novel. This is definitely done so the second half of the book and Zara's decisions will make sense, but I quickly became sick of all the shivering and hand-holding between the two. I know they're teens, but come on, touching hands isn't such a momentous thing. <b>The puppy love, pun intended, really got on my nerves.</b><br /><br />Then we get some new players on the field that really made me roll my eyes. <b>Let's just say there are more creatures than pixies and weres and it gets a little ridiculous at times.</b> It seems like Jones is just throwing whatever mythological or supernatural creatures she wants into the story. I kept waiting for a kraken to rise up from the lake or something. <br /><br /><b>Also missing from this was a bit of the creepiness that was in Need.</b> It was kind of spooky when Zara's Dad was following her around and staring at her from the woods. The pixies just feel neutered in this one, I liked it better when they were all evil, or at least had that sense of otherness about them. Astley, the other pixie king, had some potential in the beginning but toward the end I just found him boring.<br /><br />I liked the end. Sort of. I <i>need</i> to know what happens next even though the story is so haphazardly told. Thankfully, I borrowed this from work and actually read most of it on my shift so I can't say I really wasted any time or money on it. <b>I'd say borrow it from a friend or the library if you're interested, but I wouldn't buy the hardcover because it's just not worth it.</b><br /><br />My reviews of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74088731" rel="nofollow noopener">Need (Need, #1)</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106787317" rel="nofollow noopener">Entice (Need, #3)</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7555033650472983690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_86441794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86441794" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1233686-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334791106p2/1233686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86441794?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1233686-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86441794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6945521033676386221">Reading <i>Captivate</i> was so thoroughly unenjoyable that I found myself doubting how much I loved <i>Need</i> to begin with. Which is crazy, because I truly did enjoy <i>Need</i> and thought it was a great stand alone book. <br/><br/>So many probelems with <i>Captivate</i> I don't even know where to start. The story itself was....odd. There just wasn't a flow. Lot's of dangerous action scenes. Lots of pukey teen romace between Zara and Nick. But a clear plot never seemed to take shape. When everything was said and done, <i>Captivate</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6945521033676386221" style="display:none">Reading <i>Captivate</i> was so thoroughly unenjoyable that I found myself doubting how much I loved <i>Need</i> to begin with. Which is crazy, because I truly did enjoy <i>Need</i> and thought it was a great stand alone book. <br /><br />So many probelems with <i>Captivate</i> I don't even know where to start. The story itself was....odd. There just wasn't a flow. Lot's of dangerous action scenes. Lots of pukey teen romace between Zara and Nick. But a clear plot never seemed to take shape. When everything was said and done, <i>Captivate</i> read more like a filler novel. There was no blooming romance, no intrigue or mystery to discover. We only meet a handful of new characters. And while their actions definately play a role in the story, we don't spend more than a few sentences with them. <br /><br />Another issue I have with the story is the lack of growth seen in the characters. Granted, these are teens and the story takes place over a span of a fews weeks. But considering everything they have done and gone through ~ I expect a little more self discovery and character development. I think Jones expects the reader to accept the characters based on <i>Need</i>, rather than based on any insights in this story. While I found Zara to be a quirky, likeable girl in <i>Need</i>, here she is ridicuously attached to Nick and incredibly stubborn and singleminded. Zara and Nick's relationship ~ as many have pointed out ~ is barely tolerable to read about. I am ok with sappy displays of teen love ~ in small doses. Or if there is some danger or steamy scenes to balance out the, "I love you more than you love me" stuff. But <i>Captivate</i> was simply undying love. All the time. It was so bad that I was actually rooting <i>against</i> Nick in the battle scenes. Cause if he gets killed off, I won't have to read about him anymore &amp; Zara is free to pursue a more interesting guy. <br /><br />I just get the feeling that Jones wrote <i>Need</i> as a one time thing and never had intentions or ideas for a squel. But after it was published, <i>Need's</i> popularity encouraged her to quickly poop out this one. Clearly, this series is now meant to at least be a trilogy but I don't know if I will be inspired to muddle my way through another mess. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6945521033676386221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8225579392055450872">CAPTIVATE was better than NEED for a number of reasons: <br/><br/>1) Astley was introduced, and even though that may seem like a bad thing because it puts Zara into an inevitable love triangle, it's nice to get an insider pixie's perspective on things through Zara's eyes. It's nice to see that Zara puts a lot of trust into him while barely knowing him. It's nice to know she can trust him like that. Besides, Astley is awesome. And, him and Zara together make A and Z. :)<br/><br/>2) Nick started to really annoy me in</span>
  <span id="freeText8225579392055450872" style="display:none">CAPTIVATE was better than NEED for a number of reasons: <br /><br />1) Astley was introduced, and even though that may seem like a bad thing because it puts Zara into an inevitable love triangle, it's nice to get an insider pixie's perspective on things through Zara's eyes. It's nice to see that Zara puts a lot of trust into him while barely knowing him. It's nice to know she can trust him like that. Besides, Astley is awesome. And, him and Zara together make A and Z. :)<br /><br />2) Nick started to really annoy me in the beginning of this book. I'm not even sure exactly what it is about him that did that to me, but I started to lose a lot of my preconceived interest in him when Astley was introduced. Zara's caring for Nick, however, made me begin to like him again, because everything Zara experiences, I feel like I experience it right along with her (which is what I was really getting at with this #2).<br /><br />3) Zara loses a lot of her original awkwardness, which makes me glad, because that was what really turned me off of NEED. I'm glad I stuck with this series, because Zara really comes into her own in CAPTIVATE. Astley may bring some of that out of her, but it's out, nonetheless.<br /><br />4) The action was a lot more prominent in CAPTIVATE. In NEED, I felt like it was just kind of there because it needed to be, but in CAPTIVATE it was a lot more natural, like it actually should've happened instead of just happening because what-the-heck.<br /><br />What happened at the end of this book really surprised me. I thought it was going to take longer to happen, like maybe at the end of the third, or at the beginning of the fourth, but it's happened, and I can't change that.<br /><br />CAPTIVATE was more captivating than NEED, and if I hadn't have had ENTICE right there to read, I would have been extremely angry with that cliffhanger. In fact, I probably would've thrown it out my window.<br /><br /><br />Can't wait for ENTICE!</span>

<div id="review_221140324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221140324" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4581159-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322348543p2/4581159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221140324?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/4581159-jennifer">Jennifer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221140324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14151771256978439081">I loved this more than the first one! Why probably because of Astley! I'm such a sucker for the "other guy" I swear it is my downfall in books. I so rarely prefer the main guy. <br/><br/>The evil pixies are still trapped in the house in the woods. Zara and the gang continue to monitor them but something is up. A bunch of new pixies have been coming to town and they are up to something. Nick believes they should just continue to kill them off one by one. But when Zara runs into one tied up to a tree near d</span>
  <span id="freeText14151771256978439081" style="display:none">I loved this more than the first one! Why probably because of Astley! I'm such a sucker for the "other guy" I swear it is my downfall in books. I so rarely prefer the main guy. <br /><br />The evil pixies are still trapped in the house in the woods. Zara and the gang continue to monitor them but something is up. A bunch of new pixies have been coming to town and they are up to something. Nick believes they should just continue to kill them off one by one. But when Zara runs into one tied up to a tree near death, she just can't let him die. She helps Astley escape and learns that he is also a King. Her pixie blood is drawn to him and turns her skin blue and makes her faint when she is near him. Talk about falling for a guy except she is in love with Nick. <br /><br />Nick doesn't believe any pixie can be good or should be trusted. He is way to keen to just kill them all off without another thought. But the more Zara hangs out with Astley the more she believes maybe there can be good pixies. Maybe she shouldn't judge all pixies the same since we shouldn't judge all people the same. She wants there to be good ones since she is after all half pixie. I loved Astley. He was so sweet and also funny when he was naive to human ways. "You hold it right there" "Hold what?" Astley asks and I swear I think he really means it. "It's an expression," I hiss "It means stay still.'" I loved his protectiveness of Zara but didn't find it overly zealous like I did with Nick. I looked forward to his every scene. I glanced ahead just to see if he was going to be in the next scene. <br /><br />Zara's dad says that while he is stuck in that house wreak, pixies and Kings will continue to come to try to take over his territory. When another King shows up, he is far from Astley's kind. There are some truly evil pixies out there. He destroys the house and injures Nick beyond repair. Zara will do the unthinkable to save him. What I also loved about this one was the big game changer. I love when an author takes a character to a place she doesn't want to go. Zara hated pixies and never wanted to turn but sometimes it is the scary thing that is right for the character. Zara has big changes ahead of her but I am positive Astley won't let her down. This one ends of kind of abruptly. Not a total cliffhanger but everything is still up in the air unresolved. I must get the next one immediately. I felt like this one had way more action than the first and I can't wait to see where the story leads next and of course more Astley. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14151771256978439081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/922404288?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470589-kiwi-kili?shelf=love-wrecktangle">love-wrecktangle</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer922404288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer467699467571659544">Hey, guys! (It's April now because this thing has been waiting for me since April and we're pretending I'm not a procrastinator. Time machines; say whaaaaat?!) And we're going to do another Keels-reads-a-book-online-with-percentages....thingy. Or whatever. You know how this works: I start reading, making comments at various places as I go along. (With percentages so you know approx. where I am in the book.) I will be doing this ALL in one stretch, and then will go back and add GIFS later, for yo</span>
  <span id="freeText467699467571659544" style="display:none">Hey, guys! (It's April now because this thing has been waiting for me since April and we're pretending I'm not a procrastinator. Time machines; say whaaaaat?!) And we're going to do another Keels-reads-a-book-online-with-percentages....thingy. Or whatever. You know how this works: I start reading, making comments at various places as I go along. (With percentages so you know approx. where I am in the book.) I will be doing this ALL in one stretch, and then will go back and add GIFS later, for your amusement. <br><br>I know, I'm the greatest. <br><br>So. Shall we begin?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380298611ra/685939.gif" width="400" height="210" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409689560ra/11009296.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(There's some irony there....)<br><br>*****<br><br><b>1%</b> ZARA: <i>"....speechifying..." </i><br><br> .....Remind me again, are you in high school? Are you? THIS IS NOT A WOOOOORD. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409689560ra/11009297.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> ISSI: <i>"You are no longer allowed to imagine anyone is dead." </i><br><br>Somehow this seems grammatically incorrect to me...Someone help me out? If I'm wrong, I will apologize to Issi. Not to Zara, though. NEVER TO ZARA. (Actually I suspect it probably IS grammatically correct...but it still sounds weird out loud.) <br><br>And, CRIKES. I've read books when the characters are worrywarts before, but this is actually ANNOYING. I don't Need descriptions of how you are imagining your dead boyfriend, Zara dear. In fact, I do not care for him. I think you should dump him. <br><br><i>"Nick thinks insane blush mode is cute." </i> Why? Why? Why do we need a literary cliche on page two???!!! I know what to expect but...but....this is actually just CRUEL....<br><br><i>"[Wolves] are not like humans." </i> WHOA. BLOWIN' MA MIND, ZARA!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388368471ra/7812015.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>-------<br><br><b>2%</b> <i>"Winter in Maine is not fun.</i> Bad news, guys. Zara's still not over this whole "cold" thing from book one...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389683535ra/8048052.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Whoa, Dev dated a girl back in forth grade??? I don't think I knew what dating WAS in forth grade....<br><br>And wait a flippin second! This coach puts the four of these trouble makers in a group together for gym class??!!! When he yelled at them not once, but TWICE already???!!! Jeez. I wanna go to this school. You get days off in cross country for one thing, plus you can skip class apparently whenever you want. I COULD GET AWAY WITH <b>MURDER</b> (You know I could....)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409689560ra/11009298.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>---------<br><br><b>3%</b> <i>"...Now was not the time. We were in PE." </i><br><br>SINCE WHEN HAS THIS STOPPED YOU BEFORE?????!!!<br><br>----------<br><br><b>4%</b> <i>"PIXIE TIP: Pixies do not look like Tinker Bell. Although they occasionally wear tutus. Seriously--who doesn't?" </i> <br><br>Erm...is this comment supposed to make me like the characters' tone more? Because:<br><br>A--Pixie Tip: WTF???<br>and B--Who doesn't? <b>I</b> doesn't, that's who.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406921178ra/10618041.gif" width="406" height='250"' class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>----------<br><br><b>6%</b> Pixies are out and about, putting people in danger, attacking poor innocent speshul folk like Zara and making trouble. They are SO dangerous, in fact, that Nick-the-mostly-werewolf-boyfriend gets chided for patrolling on his own. This town is flippin' dangerous. <br><br>And what does our brilliant Zara do?<br><br>She goes running. BY HERSELF. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409690890ra/11009530.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><s>Most times </s>I think she's asking for this stuff. <br><br><i>"I pull out my cell phone, punch in 9-1-1 but don't hit Send. Because, seriously? What would I say?</i><br><br>Try: "Hi this is Zara Whatsherlastnameagain? and I'm down by the railroad tracks and just heard something that sounds like a person who's badly hurt. Wait for police cars to come while standing safely by the road? Sure, I can do that. <br><br>Then when she DOES call someone, who is it? Nick. Who is at work. With his phone off. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409690890ra/11009531.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah there's a reason Zara's karma is this bad....<br><br>--------<br><br><b>7%</b> Valhalla? Norse mythology? And....pixies? WTF. This is MESSED <u>UP</u>.<br><br><i>"Do you know what he is, Halfling?"</i><br><br>Um...Vampire? Please say vampire. Is it too much to ask for vampire?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409690890ra/11009532.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>-------<br><br><b>9%</b> Um...I think the pixie tip here was supposed to say that scary movies HAVE evil things in them. But the wording actually just said scary movies are evil. Hear that, folks? HORROR MOVIES ARE EVIL!!!! EM, CALL THE DOCTOR! WE WATCHED THAT "THE SHINING" TV SPECIAL! WE HAVE THE <b>TAINT</b>!!! WE IS GOING TO DIIIIIIIIIIEEEEE!!!!<br><br>---------<br><br><b>10%</b> Aw, nope. Not a vampire. Another pixie king....OOH, LOVE INTEREST #2! KEELS CALLS IT!!!! Kids, put me down for $150 in roulette. I'm feelin' good about this one...<br><br>--------<br><br><b>13%</b>Norse myths, Valhalla, Valkyries... I'm saying this RIGHT NOW: if they bastardize Loki, I will MESS THEIR SH*T <b>UP</b>!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406224864ra/10522158.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, well, and Zara's right about googling Valkyrie and getting the Tom Cruise film first, but the SECOND HIT in Wikipedia is about the Norse bits. And wouldn't you put that in there to begin with? Valkyrie + Norse? (Huh, sounds like a bad romance...) Just to save on time?<br><br>-------<br><br><b>15%</b> <i>"No. Nick or my grandma would have smelled him there. You know their noses." </i><br><br>NO, WITH THEIR TOES!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382362818ra/5847892.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>------<br><br><b>17%</b> Okay, so, bitch move here, but hear me out: I kinda agree with Zara's pixie dad on this one. Her mom decided to sleep with him, decides not to stay with him. The pixies only become evil psychos without a queen...He HAD a queen. She DITCHED him. If their biology is written for them to need to drink blood (hehe, vampires...) when they don't have a queen...Doesn't this make things sorta not their fault?<br><br>I mean, don't get me wrong, it's their fault for DOING the deeds all in all, but isn't it Zara's mom's fault for being like "see ya later, husband o mine. I'm marrying a human instead! Whoo!"<br><br>Zara should make up a word for pixie-sympathy. She has a made up word for everything else....<br><br>And Zara, DON'T BE FLIPPING CONTRADICTORY!!! If you're gonna be all chill about having a werewolf for a boyfriend, (<i>"He is NOT an animal!"</i>) then you're gonna hafta get over the pixie-dad thing as well...Because one of those things IS stranger than the other. <br><br>And no, it's not the pixie bit. <br><br><i>"The whole 'Nick protecting me' thing drives me insane. I can protect myself." </i> <br><br>OH NO YOU MOST CERTAIN CAN<b>NOT</b>!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409690890ra/11009533.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>-----<br><br><b>20%</b> Blond man waiting in the road who you hope isn't there for you? Well is he hot, Zara? Tell us if he's hot. That will make figuring it out SOOO much easier...<br><br>-----<br><br><b>21%</b> <i>"...or I've lost forty IQ points or something..."</i><br><br>And trust me, kid; those were 40 points you could NOT afford to lose...<br><br>And yep, he was there for her. He's now hot by default. <br><br>----<br><br><b>26%</b> Do-gooderness.<br><br>.....Is it my turn to make up a word now? Please? Pretty please cherries and sprinkles? (Ironically I donate these two ice cream toppings because I hate them...)<br><br>Also apparently muppets don't USUALLY kill people. Well that's a relief. Honestly I'd be MUCH more worried about having a muppet kill me than a pixie. I'm a chick, so pixies wouldn't drink my blood they'd if anything just try to marry me. That's a lot easier to handle than a giant Cookie Monster blundering at you screaming COOOOKKIEEEEEEE in a way that makes you believe YOU are the cookie he wants to eat now. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385782366ra/7226780.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>THIS COULD BE <u>YOU</u>.<br><br>Also Grover is a pyromaniac. And death by fire sounds harsh, man. <br><br>----<br><br><b>28%</b> Is Nick's only purpose in this book to BE MAN, call her baby, and protect/stalk things?<br><br>-----<br><br><b>29%</b> Hehe. Zara makes a list of illegal things they've done. ON PAPER. Not even hidden away on her computer....Better hope those useless Maine cops don't find THAT little slip up...<br><br>-----<br><br><b>30%</b> <i>"Nick's fingers stroke my skin.</i> <br><br>Creeeeep-eeer.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404854358ra/10289355.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also: why are these children obsessed with bagels???<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409690890ra/11009534.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>-----<br><br><b>33%</b> <i>"'Look at my lips! They are too thin! They hardly even count as lips...'"</i><br><br>HEY WAIT A MINUTE! <b>I</b> HAVE THINISH/SMALL LIPS!!!<br><br>Don't be hating on people with little mouths. Small on the outside, CAVERNOUS on the inside...<br><br>-----<br><br><b>34%</b> Okay, so are books like TV shows now? Do authors get extra cash for dropping as many brand names as possible?<br><br>Jus' wonderin'. <br><br>-----<br><br><b>40%</b> ZARA: <i>"And why has nobody told me this before?</i><br><br>Oh, Zara. CLEARLY because it wasn't necessary to the plot then. It is NOW....<br><br>-----<br><br><b>41%</b> Aw...poor Zara's havin' a meltdown....she's so SPESHUL, she can't even handle it...she's feelin' a bit...BLUE! Hahahahahahaha!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408947261ra/10914586.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*Cough* Okay I'm done now. (Blue...heh. For those of you who haven't read this book--and are thanking your lucky stars you didn't--Zara starts turning blue in the book. Yeah, actually full-on blue skin. I didn't want you to be left out of the joke. I KNOW. I'm so nice...)<br><br>------<br><br><b>44%</b> KEELS' PREDICTION NUMBER TWO: SOMETHING WILL HAPPEN CONVENIENTLY SO ZARA WILL HAVE AN EXCUSE TO KISS THE HOT BLOND PIXIE AND THEN BECOME A PIXIE HERSELF. BUT DON'T WORRY. SHE WILL STILL MAKE THINGS WORK WITH NICK.<br><br>Apparently pixies smell like Dove soap.<br><br>Guys.......? <i>Guys.....? </i>CONSPIRACY THEORY ALERT!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/348590.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>-----<br><br><b>53%</b> Pixie Federation. They. Flipping. Have. A. <i>Pixie</i> Federation. <br><br>Anywho, there's ANOTHER pixie king coming for Zara...(Three's a crowd folks)...who apparently is as evil as evil is evil. <br><br>I WANT HIM. NOW. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390300223ra/8186716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>-----<br><br><b>55%</b> <i>"We fall asleep there, curled up together, fully clothed obviously because we haven't actually had actual sex yet..."</i><br><br>Yeah, but have you had NON-actual sex yet? That's the REAL question, Zara...<br><br>-----<br><br><b>58%</b> Ooooh, spooky. Things smell like death. Tell me, Nick, what does death smell like? Is it like pain, which apparently demands to be felt??<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409691379i/11009584.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>----<br><br><b>63%</b> Bum badda ba bum, bum badda BA bum, bum badda BA bum, bum budda DAAAA! (That's Ride of the Valkyries for all you who didn't know.) And YEAH!! That's right!! The valkyrie just showed up to snatch Nicky-boy, giving us a perfectly good excuse to now kiss hot-blond Astley, yeah!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409691186ra/11009558.gif" width="400" height="262" class="gr-hostedUserImg">/&gt;<br><br>----<br><br><b>66%</b> <i>"My cell. Call it if you need me," he says. "I won't need you," I tell him...."But thanks." </i><br><br>YES SHE DOES, ASTELY!!! SHE DOES NEED YOU!!! NEEEEEEED. <br><br>Well screw you, Zara. Hey guys, guess who just went into the woods by herself again? Ya-huh, ZARA. And guess who swung in to her rescue? Yeah, uh-huh, ASTLEY. <br><br>SIGH HEAVILY. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408148341ra/10814477.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>----<br><br><b>68%</b> Astley's completely right, Zara; we all need to be rescued some times...Just you more than anyone else. <br><br>----<br><br><b>69%</b> Oh my gollywollydoodlealltheday. Oh goodness. Oh hilarious hysteria. <br><br>The evil pixie's name is...Frank. ITS FRANK. FRAAAAAAAANK!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403079739ra/10033469.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409691186ra/11009559.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384595594ra/6909520.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>----<br><br><b>70%</b> They are now speaking about Odin and Thor. Let me reiterate:<br><br>If they bastardize Loki......I WILL MESS THEIR FACES UP.<br><br>----<br><br><b>74%</b> Geez, Zara, of COURSE Nick's parents are dead. You hadn't figured that out yet??? Crikes...<br><br>Wait a second, where does this kid LIVE????<br><br>----<br><br><b>82%</b> <i>"I'm not most people,"</i> says Zara. <br><br>TRUST US, ZARA, WE KNOW. <br><br>----<br><br><b>86%</b><br><br>Um....you don't cook spaghetti in a pan. <br><br>Oh, also, Keel's Prediction #3 or whatever we're on: There will be a completely normal explanation as to why Cassidy and Dev are hanging out that doesn't have to do with LOOOOVE so Issi and Dev can still be an item. <br><br>----<br><br><b>87%</b> Not only is Zara a pixie now, she's even a SPESHUL pixie. Because she can heal in superfast time. Sigh. Goody for you, Zara. Goody for you... (Uh, oh guys. Looks like I have glitter envy...)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409691186ra/11009560.gif" width="300" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>----<br><br><b>95%</b> Yup. Cassidy is part elf. She was chillin' with Dev to learn the secrets of the trade. S'all cool now, bros!<br><br>Oh, and about five sentences later Issi announces she and Devyn are a couple now. Brilliant. <br><br>----<br><br><b>98%</b> Wait a minute....they just learned that Nick is still alive, the fate of the world rests in their hands, and there is probably a giant battle-leading-to-a-possible-apocalypse-coming and they head to a DANCE???!! A FLIPPING SCHOOL DANCE???!!!<br><br>What is the world coming to??<br><br>----<br><br>Well then. WELL THEN. <b>WELL THEN</b>. Looks like we're done. <br><br>So...what was the point of this book, actually? What was the plot? <br><br>WAS there a plot???<br><br>Hmmm....I shall ponder this....At least they didn't bastardize Loki (my warnings SHALL be heard). And at least I got a good pot of new money for my hypothetical bank account because of all my predictability-ness.<br><br>Yay! Keels finally got to make up a word too!!! Aw, so happy now. <br><br>See y'all later when I put the GIFS in...<br><br><br><br><br>(And while you wait, go check out my review of the first book....)</span>

<div id="review_64335313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64335313" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64335313?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64335313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3155789502149233025">I Need more! I was completely Captivate-d..... I devoured this novel. This is such a fun and entertaining series, I absolutely loved it. <br/><br/>Zara, my favorite phobic is back, and even more entangled in a pixie web. I did not see the story developing this way at all. The introduction of Valhalla, took the story to a whole new level and I can not wait to see what Jones has in store for us next. <br/><br/>The plot was an emotional roller coaster, I was up, I was down, I was thrown for a loop and it came screechi</span>
  <span id="freeText3155789502149233025" style="display:none">I Need more! I was completely Captivate-d..... I devoured this novel. This is such a fun and entertaining series, I absolutely loved it. <br /><br />Zara, my favorite phobic is back, and even more entangled in a pixie web. I did not see the story developing this way at all. The introduction of Valhalla, took the story to a whole new level and I can not wait to see what Jones has in store for us next. <br /><br />The plot was an emotional roller coaster, I was up, I was down, I was thrown for a loop and it came screeching to a stop all too quickly. I mean really! How could you do this to me Carrie Jones, you KNOW what I am talking about! <br /><br />Loved the new character of Astley. I still don’t have him figured out and I think that is exactly where Jones wants readers to be. Is he good, is he bad? Is he playing Zara for a fool, or is he really there to give a helping hand? I DON’T KNOW! And I can’t stand it. <br /><br />Overall Captivate is a fantastic read! Intriguing characters, engrossing plot, blood thirsty pixies... can it get any better?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3155789502149233025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_70277910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70277910" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2515913-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309066626p2/2515913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70277910?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/2515913-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2515913-kate?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70277910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer483100358735603583">May contain spoilers from Need, please read at your own risk.<br/><br/>Captivate was an amazingly entertaining read. Like its predecessor, Need, the novel is full of creative elements. The words fly off the pages, sucking readers into this unique world that Jones has created. The plot picks up right where Need left off: Zara is beginning to settle into her new life with her grandmother, her relationship with Nick is going strong, everything seems to be a positive... except Zara's father. He and the other </span>
  <span id="freeText483100358735603583" style="display:none">May contain spoilers from Need, please read at your own risk.<br /><br />Captivate was an amazingly entertaining read. Like its predecessor, Need, the novel is full of creative elements. The words fly off the pages, sucking readers into this unique world that Jones has created. The plot picks up right where Need left off: Zara is beginning to settle into her new life with her grandmother, her relationship with Nick is going strong, everything seems to be a positive... except Zara's father. He and the other pixies are a sore spot that Zara just cannot ignore. And to top everything off, a new pixie king emerges causing Zara to question everything.<br /><br />While this novel is missing a few elements that made Need so special for me (Zara's continuous listing of phobias and the creepiness factor), Jones more than makes up for it through her usage of powerful emotions. This novel will make you laugh, make you sigh, and more than likely, make you cry.<br /><br />In regards to the characters, I am happy to report that for the most part, they remained true to their personalities: Zara is still her phobia-loving self, Nick is still a little over possessive, etc. However, it is the newer characters made me scratch my head a few times while trying to understand their purpose. Astley is a prime example of this. While he has the possibility to be a wonderful, sexy character, he can sometimes come off a little boring. Yes, this is his introduction novel, but I wanted to get to know him better... I wanted to see if you can trust a pixie. Unfortunately, with this novel, readers are only able to put out their feelers for him, and the truth behind his character and motivation will not be revealed at least until the next novel. Having enjoyed novels similar to these, I am very curious to see what path Jones will take with Astley. I have a few hunches, but I will have to wait and see if I am right.<br /><br />While I did not overall love Captivate as much as Need, Captivate still has a lot going for it. There is plenty of romance, sadness, changes in character development, etc. For those of you who enjoyed Need, Captivate is a must read. For those who have been a little hesitant about reading this series, I say, give it a try. It is a truly amazing series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="483100358735603583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_135139223" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135139223" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135139223?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135139223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9872569400659458963">“What happens to us all is partially up to me and it is my job, my duty, to protect my friends”<br/><br/>Zara, Nick, Issie, and Devyn maintain a tenuous hold on normality. Sure, Zara is half-pixie, Nick is a werewolf and Devyn is a were-eagle, and the entire gang keeps a watch for new pixies, but life goes on. Until a new pixie king arrives warning of danger to come.<br/><br/><b>NOTE:</b> After reading the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136028127' rel='nofollow noopener'>third book</a> and being hugely disappointed - enough to sell this book back! - I have gone back and downrated this to th</span>
  <span id="freeText9872569400659458963" style="display:none">“What happens to us all is partially up to me and it is my job, my duty, to protect my friends”<br /><br />Zara, Nick, Issie, and Devyn maintain a tenuous hold on normality. Sure, Zara is half-pixie, Nick is a werewolf and Devyn is a were-eagle, and the entire gang keeps a watch for new pixies, but life goes on. Until a new pixie king arrives warning of danger to come.<br /><br /><b>NOTE:</b> After reading the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136028127" rel="nofollow noopener">third book</a> and being hugely disappointed - enough to sell this book back! - I have gone back and downrated this to three stars.<br /><br />I Liked:<br />The primary new character in the book, Astley, was very welcomed. Even though it is obvious he is supposed to be part of the budding Romantic Triangle (see below for my thoughts on that), I felt he brought interesting dimension to the book. Up to this point, all the pixies that have been shown are mean, evil, controlled by their “needs”. Astley shows the Big Four (Zara, Nick, Issie, and Devyn) that pixies don't have to be evil...they have a choice.<br /><br />Which brings me to the amazing themes in this book. I don't normally talk about themes in a review, but there are so many good, important lessons in here (unlike in many other teenaged vampire romance novels) that I just have to spend some time talking about them.<br /><br />Firstly, Zara may be dating Nick, she may love him dearly, but never once does she let him govern her life. In fact, she even declares (page 195): “He didn't make my choices for me when he was here and he's not going to start now”. This is a great message to young women, a counter to our culture and other media that tell women that A) they need a man (something else this book also counters, see page 268 and 120) and B) once they have a man, the man makes all the decisions. This is one big reason I adore Zara as a character. She is independent, she makes her own thoughts, she takes life in her own hands and actually does something to change her destiny and save her friends.<br /><br />The second big theme is bigotry. Let's face it, before Astley arrives, the Big Four believe all pixies are inherently bad and can't be redeemed. Hence why capturing them in an iron clad house is okay—because they can't change from their evil selves. The best way I can detail this change in thought is to quote the book once again (page 233): “Bigotry isn't that straight and easy. It isn't there and then suddenly gone. It's like a bad germ waiting to pounce and infect you even when you think an antibiotic has eradicated it from your system.”<br /><br />Carrie Jones used Captivate to include more Norse mythology, a very welcome change of pace from the oversaturation of “traditional” vampires and faerie mythology. This is the first time I've read of Valhalla and Valkyries in a young adult novel, as well as were-tigers, eages, and bears. I honestly can't wait to see what else she includes and definitely want to do more research into Norse mythology.<br /><br />I also liked how Jones added more action to this book. The second half especially gets pretty intense—even Issie, our dear sweet girl, takes up a crossbow to fend off pixies attacking Betty's house (talk about intense!).<br /><br />I Didn't Like:<br />One of the things that made Need such a wonderful book was its decidedly ominous, creepy tone. It was less “urban fantasy” and borderline horror (Stephen King, Dean Koontz). Well, that sense of foreboding is pretty much gone in Captivate. There is no building tension, building horror, no wanting to peer behind your shoulder in paranoia. It's just straight-laced young adult urban fantasy.<br /><br />While I liked Astley as a character, I groaned at the inclusion of the obligatory Romantic Triangle. Why does every novel have to have two guys competing for our heroine's affections? I wasn't that fond of Nick (and again, I like Astley), but I am so tired of treading this road. No matter how much I want Zara to go with Astley, I am afraid (per Romantic Lead Rule #57) that it will all be for naught and Zara will end up with Nick in the end.<br /><br />And the writing! It wasn't that long ago that I read Need, in which Carrie Jones handled the first person present really well (it isn't that easy to use). Here, it is literally like I am reading a sixth grade short story assignment. I try not to dole that complaint out a lot (it tends to lose its meaning), but seriously, the writing here is positively atrocious and embarrassing. Sentences are constructed at about the third grade reading level. “I saw the cat jump up the tree. The cat was yellow and fat.” This strikes me as odd A) because Need wasn't written that way and B) this is in the young adult section, not the children. And in case you think I'm lying, here are some excerpts that I happened to note:<br /><br /><blockquote>Page 118: “I am not who you should be worried about.” [said Astley] I shake my head. “...Of course you're who I should worry about.” (Okay, I know it's dialogue, but why does Zara all of a sudden phrase things exactly like Astley?)<br /><br />Page 168: “Something wet falls from my face and hits his cheek. Tears.” No duh, really? Tears? Let me guess: they are also Zara's tears! D'oh! This sort of “revelation” or “style” is repeated ad nauseum.<br /><br />Page 196: “ I will shower. I will shower and think. I will shower and think and not shake. I will shower and think and not shake and I will imagine what it'll be like to see Nick again.” Good GOD IN HEAVEN! I get the point! No need to repeat the same thing in triplicate to make sure the audience knows.</blockquote><br /><br />In the first half, the story is incredibly boring. I can see where Jones is including hints to what is to come (Valkyries, Valhalla, Astley, etc.), but while waiting for this interesting stuff to take place, we have to suffer through romantic melodrama between Devyn and Issie and Cassidy (rolls eyes) and the romantic googly eyes that Zara and Nick exchange (just old after awhile).<br /><br />Betty and Mrs. Nix are absent for a lot of the book, which was a shame. Both of them were really interesting. I also kept wondering what happened to Zara's pixie father.<br /><br />Dialogue/Sexual Situations/Violence:<br />Cr*p, da**, and he** are as extreme as it gets.<br />Zara and Nick exchange kisses (Zara explicitly says they haven't had sex). Devyn, Issie, and Cassidy are part of their own Romantic Triangle. There is the needs the pixies have, which could be construed possibly as sexual needs (not sure though).<br />This book is way more violent than the last one. Zara kills at least three pixies, and it is fairly detailed. Nick is abducted; Zara is injured on two occasions.<br /><br />Overall:<br />Compared to Need, this is a disappointment. The creepy edge is gone and the writing itself has plummeted. Even the plot starts off weakly. Fortunately, the second half and the inclusion of very empowering themes of acceptance and independence make up for the beginning and the clunky writing. Plus, Jones begins to hint at an enormous battle, which is definitely more interesting than the objectives of other teenaged urban fantasy (“Does so-and-so get X or Y?”). 3.5 stars rounded generously to 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9872569400659458963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6745029925731100085">Does the title speak true?, you might ask yourself. The answer is no. I was not captivated. Ok, so I'm not hard-core feminist, but I am on a minor level, and Nick got under my skin so much. He called Zara 'Baby' and 'babe' so many times that I was tempted to clock him over the head. He is always telling her what to do and all, "No,no I can do it, but you can't becaue you are a puny woman. Leave the pixie slaying to us big men."<br/>How could she stand that? I mean, honsetly, I liked Nick in the first</span>
  <span id="freeText6745029925731100085" style="display:none">Does the title speak true?, you might ask yourself. The answer is no. I was not captivated. Ok, so I'm not hard-core feminist, but I am on a minor level, and Nick got under my skin so much. He called Zara 'Baby' and 'babe' so many times that I was tempted to clock him over the head. He is always telling her what to do and all, "No,no I can do it, but you can't becaue you are a puny woman. Leave the pixie slaying to us big men."<br />How could she stand that? I mean, honsetly, I liked Nick in the first book, but when a mysterious, handsome pixie king enters the picture, i was like, "YES!" Astley (said pixie king) was kind and generous, but I got kinda peeved cause he was so mellow all the time. Oh, and Zara's undying loyalty to Nick, even when something bad happens (don't wanna spoil it) is rather sickening. and the ever - infuriating line, "I can't exixt without him!" is just so.....ugh. I will give the book so credit in that there were several twists, and unexpectedness, but it was really hard to focus on that with all of Zara's crap. </span>

<div id="review_978252304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer978252304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1391842418734486055"><b>Actual rating - 2.5</b><br/><br/>I was hoping this would be better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4070493.Need__Need___1_' title='Need (Need, #1) by Carrie Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>Need</a>, but unfortunately, it wasn't.<br/><br/>Zara annoyed me in the last book, and she annoyed me just as much in this one.<br/>She continued to chant phobias like she did in book one, but thankfully, she didn't do it as much in this one. <br/><br/>The book just bored me, and i couldn't get interested in it at all. When the "interesting" things happened, i didn't really care. <br/>The only thing that i liked was the ending - Not what happened at the end, just the fact</span>
  <span id="freeText1391842418734486055" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating - 2.5</b><br /><br />I was hoping this would be better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4070493.Need__Need___1_" title="Need (Need, #1) by Carrie Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Need</a>, but unfortunately, it wasn't.<br /><br />Zara annoyed me in the last book, and she annoyed me just as much in this one.<br />She continued to chant phobias like she did in book one, but thankfully, she didn't do it as much in this one. <br /><br />The book just bored me, and i couldn't get interested in it at all. When the "interesting" things happened, i didn't really care. <br />The only thing that i liked was the ending - Not what happened at the end, just the fact that i had finished. <br /><br />Overall, Slow, dull, and had an annoying main character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1391842418734486055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_84383309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84383309" />
    <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales"><img alt="Dark Faerie Tales" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253675501p2/2766672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84383309?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark Faerie Tales" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales">Dark Faerie Tales</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84383309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2012512627377397981">Quick & Dirty: This is a fierce tale that will evoke every emotion and leave you wanting more.<br/><br/>Opening Sentence: Sometimes there are these bizarre people who actually like physical education class.<br/><br/>The Review:<br/><br/>Our favorite lovable phobic is back. Once again, Zara takes the reader on an amazing journey filled with heartbreak and death. We get a glimpse at some of Zara's new phobias, but we also get a "Top Ten Things to Remember When Dealing with Pixies" list, as well as some pixie tips and hints. Ca</span>
  <span id="freeText2012512627377397981" style="display:none">Quick &amp; Dirty: This is a fierce tale that will evoke every emotion and leave you wanting more.<br /><br />Opening Sentence: Sometimes there are these bizarre people who actually like physical education class.<br /><br />The Review:<br /><br />Our favorite lovable phobic is back. Once again, Zara takes the reader on an amazing journey filled with heartbreak and death. We get a glimpse at some of Zara's new phobias, but we also get a "Top Ten Things to Remember When Dealing with Pixies" list, as well as some pixie tips and hints. Captivate picks up shortly after the ending of Need. Zara and The Scooby Gang know that their previous pixie solution is only a temporary fix. Zara struggles with her decisions and starts to question how pixies should be treated. The deadly pixies are becoming increasingly harder to detain, and more are flocking to Bedford, Maine at an alarming rate. Matters further intensify when a new pixie king arrives looking to claim Zara as his queen, as well as takeover the territory. The new king is unlike any other pixie that Zara has met. This completely throws her emotions into a tailspin. She foolishly puts her trust in him knowing that it could prove to be disastrous. Zara is willing to give up everything and become the one thing that she fears the most. With an impending pixie war looming, Zara starts to realize the effects that her decisions have caused. A bloody power struggle is underway and there is nothing that Zara can do to stop it. Zara's motivations and conflicts really drive this absorbing tale.<br /><br />Ms. Jones also introduces a few new characters. I absolutely loved Astley. I'm not sure that I entirely trust him, but he does have some redeeming qualities. While he did help Zara in many ways, doing so also served his purposes. I definitely want to get to know him better.<br /><br />I was a bit surprised by the ending. The book ends on a cliffhanger, leaving room to have major plot points continued in the next installment. I can't wait to read about the events that unfold between Astley, Zara, and Nick. It's so clear to see that the dynamics of Zara's relationship with Nick have been changed forever. Ms. Jones creates intriguing and compelling characters, and makes you care about them.<br /><br />Overall, Captivate is definitely worth reading. I really enjoyed visiting this world again. It will keep you engaged and guessing at every turn. Ms. Jones continues to do an excellent job of world-building. Captivate continued to build on the established lore from the first book in the series, Need, as well as introducing a new mythology. With the vulnerable king's needs spinning out of control and ravenous and rampaging pixies on the loose, Bedford, Maine is deadlier than ever.<br /><br />Notable Scene:<br /><br />He pulls me into his chest, but I've already seen. I've already seen and it's stuck inside my brain like panic and terror, like a bad horror movie image that won't let go: bodies twisted on the marble floor; blood splashed across walls like arteries have been cut; hands severed in the middle of the floor not connected to anything; eyes open; mouths stuck in screams. I yank away from Nick and stare. Then I start moving. I hold my breath as I go from one corpse to another.<br /><br />FTC Advisory: Bloomsbury provided me with an ARC of Captivate. No goody bags, sponsorships, "material connections," or bribes were exchanged for my review. In addition, I don't receive affiliate fees for anything purchased via links from my site.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2012512627377397981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_87219064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87219064" />
    <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy"><img alt="All Things Urban Fantasy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320345194p2/2732683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87219064?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="All Things Urban Fantasy" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy">All Things Urban Fantasy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy?shelf=reviewed-by-abigail">reviewed-by-abigail</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87219064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer538469575385022128">Review courtesy of AllThingsUrbanFantasy.blogspot.com<br/><br/> One of the reasons I enjoyed Need (the first book in this series) so much was because of the honest and thoughtful voice of the protagonist, Zara. She was understandably melancholy (read my review HERE), but completely lacking in self pity. She was a realistic teenager without any of the CW-esque superficiality. In Captivate, after surviving a series of earth shattering experiences, and nearly loosing her life, I expected Zara to be even more</span>
  <span id="freeText538469575385022128" style="display:none">Review courtesy of AllThingsUrbanFantasy.blogspot.com<br /><br /> One of the reasons I enjoyed Need (the first book in this series) so much was because of the honest and thoughtful voice of the protagonist, Zara. She was understandably melancholy (read my review HERE), but completely lacking in self pity. She was a realistic teenager without any of the CW-esque superficiality. In Captivate, after surviving a series of earth shattering experiences, and nearly loosing her life, I expected Zara to be even more grounded and serious about the new direction her life had taken. Unfortunately the older and wiser Zara is notably absent this time out.<br /><br />**Spoilers if you haven’t read Need**<br /><br />Captivate begins with Zara and Co. still hunting stray pixies and trapping them inside the iron enforced hidden mansion with her pixie king father. Zara is increasingly anxious about her werewolf boyfriend Nick’s solo missions, while he is equally upset by her sudden softening towards one particular pixie, Astley. Astley, a pixie king himself, challenges Zara’s long held belief that all pixies are evil. He makes no secret of his desires to have her as his pixie queen, but he does not force her either. He encourages her to consider the fate of the humans she loves as they are in danger once again with more and more pixies arriving and the reality of the temporary ‘pixie prison’ inevitable collapse, not to mention another king whose evil surpasses any that Zara has imagined.<br /><br />Captivate introduces some new mythology into the Need universe, specifically Norse mythology. Valhalla, valkyries, the great battle of Ragnarök, and the god Odin. We don’t get a full explanation of how this added mythology will impact the already established world building. That information seems to be reserved for the as yet untitled Need book 3.<br /><br />The basic plot is a fun continuation of the original premise of Zara trying to come to terms with both her human and pixie heritage and the nature of good and evil within all of us, but because of the lack of depth with the main characters, this sequel seems somewhat shallow. Zara and her friends are now inordinately consumed with junior high-ish angst over their respective crushes. The dialogue (which was so smart and snappy in Need) is now bogged down with plenty freaking ’s and cool ’s etc. And Zara makes several TSTL (To stupid to live) choices that really grated. I did enjoy the love triangle that was created with the introduction of Astley (I predict a Team Nick vs Team Astley war will be ensuing, and for the record: I’m going with Team Astley).<br /><br />Despite some significant flaws, Captivate is still a good read though no where near as captivating as Need. Carrie Jones proved her talent to me with the first book in this series, and while the second effort was a bit of a stumble, I’m hoping the third book will more than make up for it.<br /><br />Sexual Content: (YA books receive a more thorough breakdown) Kissing<br /><br />My Rating: 3 out of 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="538469575385022128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_92220383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92220383" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2919909-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404322642p2/2919909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92220383?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2919909-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92220383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15929109513264137645">Geez, what a mess. Where do I start? <br/><br/>First-Setting up the story: When did Zara become valley girl in her speaking? And when did the words "Baby" and "Oh (insert name here)" become manly for a werewolf?! And then you have Devyn appearing to be cheating on Issie? And all in the first two chapters? This is wrong on so many levels and completely turned me off before I even knew what was going on in the book.<br/><br/>Second-Writing Style: I don't remember Need being written like Captivate. If you like short c</span>
  <span id="freeText15929109513264137645" style="display:none">Geez, what a mess. Where do I start? <br /><br />First-Setting up the story: When did Zara become valley girl in her speaking? And when did the words "Baby" and "Oh (insert name here)" become manly for a werewolf?! And then you have Devyn appearing to be cheating on Issie? And all in the first two chapters? This is wrong on so many levels and completely turned me off before I even knew what was going on in the book.<br /><br />Second-Writing Style: I don't remember Need being written like Captivate. If you like short choppy sentences with bad grammar, then this is the book for you. Sentences such as "We actually haven't had actual sex yet" (yes, this is word for word) Or "He did something. He called 911." (yes, word for word again) - they lack just about everything I've taught in writing lessons to my 5th grade class. Oh, and dialogue lacked contractions so it sounded fake - another pet peeve of mine. <br /><br />THIS WILL GET SPOILER-ISH - STOP IF YOU HAVE NOT READ NEED<br /><br />Third-Plot eerily familiar: Need was criticized for being too much like Twilight - Zara moves from hot southern town to the far cold north to small town to live with Grandmother that she barely knows. Zara finds out weres and pixies exist. Zara gets caught in battle and yada, yada, yada (insert spoons and forks here)(okay, I just through that in for giggles) (but yes, it's still totally absurd that forks was the weapon of choice to defeat the bad guys). In Captivate - Zara faces a big decision and the way it was written reminded me a of a little book called Breaking Dawn and well, being the 4th book of Twilight, just a little something to make you think...hmmmmm.<br /><br />OKAY - SO NOW THAT I HAVE THAT OFF MY CHEST - THE GOOD PARTS<br /><br />While I HATED Nick in this book because he was a total pansy with his "Baby" talk and gag me this and gag me that - Astley totally kicks ass. That is what a male MC should be like. Keep him around. <br /><br />There is a chapter near the end that isn't written choppy!! I went back and checked and it actually flowed. Kudos!<br /><br />The cover is beautiful just like Need's cover.<br /><br />And um...so I like the killing and gore stuff that finally happened. It livened the book up to the point that it earned a star back.<br /><br />Will I read a book 3 if it's coming out? Probably not. Captivate just wasn't for me - I need a bit more sustenance to a story as well as a deeper level of writing to keep my interest on a book-likable level. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15929109513264137645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_589564659" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/589564659" />
    <a title="Jeninne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17933811-jeninne"><img alt="Jeninne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364530237p2/17933811.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/589564659?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeninne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeninne" href="/user/show/17933811-jeninne">Jeninne</a>
      </span>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17933811-jeninne?shelf=weak-female-lead">weak-female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17933811-jeninne?shelf=unnecessary-love-triangle">unnecessary-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17933811-jeninne?shelf=teenage-angst">teenage-angst</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer589564659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13114406522658074284">There is a standard to which I judge fantasy YA books. I ask myself, is this worse than Twilight? If the answer is no, I keep reading. The answer this time was nearly yes.<br/><br/>The fact is, there were so many problems with this book I rarely felt like a book. It felt like a rough draft of a novice writer looking to get published. There was no fluidity to the writing. There was certainly nothing engaging. And the characters. God, the characters.<br/><br/>I'll admit, Zara had charm in the first book. She was litt</span>
  <span id="freeText13114406522658074284" style="display:none">There is a standard to which I judge fantasy YA books. I ask myself, is this worse than Twilight? If the answer is no, I keep reading. The answer this time was nearly yes.<br /><br />The fact is, there were so many problems with this book I rarely felt like a book. It felt like a rough draft of a novice writer looking to get published. There was no fluidity to the writing. There was certainly nothing engaging. And the characters. God, the characters.<br /><br />I'll admit, Zara had charm in the first book. She was little headstrong, and short tempered, but she's a teen, so I'm willing to let a lot slide. But this time around she's just plain annoying. She doesn't listen to reason. she acts without thinking. She gets mad and storms off. And worst of all, she goes from a fairly independent girl, to hanging off the end of her boyfriend's arm. Apparently now she can't do anything without his approval, or at least asking forgiveness after, and without his attention she's likely to wilt. He's now the focus of her world, which turns her into nothing but a prop, and destroys the entire book.<br /><br />And Nick? He seriously comes close to Edward Cullen status in this book with how controlling he is. He was relatively likable in the first book. But now he's telling her what to do, and trying to control her thoughts and shaming her for thinking independently and overall being a total asshole. I nearly got out the pompoms when we were introduced to the new love interest, Astley. Astley had more personally in twenty pages than Nick had in two books. <br /><br />All the other character felt flat, or were dull, or unlikeable/uninteresting. The plot felt like nothing but a setup for the next books, or maybe like the author didn't know where it was going. It's a mess.<br /><br />The first book had serious problems too, but it actually had charm, which is why I sort of, kind of, a little bit enjoyed it, and picked up the sequel. This book has no charm, no appeal, and I warrant the only people who'll like this book are sixteen or haven't ever had a boyfriend and idealize the concept. I feel like that should be a warning on the book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13114406522658074284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
